<p><b>Rutherford Birchard Hayes</b> (October 4, 1822&#160;– January 17, 1893) was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States" title="List of Presidents of the United States">19th</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> (1877–1881). As president, he oversaw the end of <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Era_of_the_United_States" title="Reconstruction Era of the United States" class="mw-redirect">Reconstruction</a>, began the efforts that led to civil service reform, and attempted to reconcile the divisions left over from the Civil War and Reconstruction.</p>
<p>Hayes, an attorney in Ohio, became city solicitor of <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a> from 1858 to 1861. When the Civil War began, he left a fledgling political career to join the <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">Union Army</a> as an officer. Hayes was wounded five times, most seriously at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_South_Mountain" title="Battle of South Mountain">Battle of South Mountain</a>; he earned a reputation for bravery in combat and was promoted to the rank of major general. After the war, he served in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">U.S. Congress</a> from 1865 to 1867 as a <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="History of the Republican Party (United States)" class="mw-redirect">Republican</a>. Hayes left Congress to run for <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Ohio" title="Governor of Ohio" class="mw-redirect">Governor of Ohio</a> and was elected to two consecutive terms, from 1868 to 1872, and then to a third term, from 1876 to 1877.</p>
<p>In 1876, Hayes was <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1876" title="United States presidential election, 1876">elected president</a> in one of the most contentious and confused elections in national history. He lost the popular vote to <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="History of the Democratic Party (United States)" class="mw-redirect">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Samuel_J._Tilden" title="Samuel J. Tilden">Samuel J. Tilden</a> but he won an intensely disputed electoral college vote after a Congressional commission awarded him twenty contested electoral votes. The result was the <a href="/wiki/Compromise_of_1877" title="Compromise of 1877">Compromise of 1877</a>, in which the Democrats acquiesced to Hayes's election and Hayes ended all U.S. military involvement in Southern politics.</p>
<p>Hayes believed in meritocratic government, equal treatment without regard to race, and improvement through education. He ordered federal troops to crush the <a href="/wiki/Great_Railroad_Strike_of_1877" title="Great Railroad Strike of 1877">Great Railroad Strike of 1877</a>. He implemented modest civil service reforms that laid the groundwork for further reform in the 1880s and 1890s. He vetoed the <a href="/wiki/Bland%E2%80%93Allison_Act" title="Bland–Allison Act">Bland–Allison Act</a>, which would have put silver money into circulation and raised prices, insisting that maintenance of the gold standard was essential to economic recovery. His policy toward Western Indians anticipated the assimilationist program of the <a href="/wiki/Dawes_Act" title="Dawes Act">Dawes Act</a> of 1887.</p>
<p>Hayes kept his pledge not to run for re-election, retired to his home in Ohio, and became an advocate of social and educational reform. Biographer <a href="/wiki/Ari_Hoogenboom" title="Ari Hoogenboom">Ari Hoogenboom</a> says his greatest achievement was to restore popular faith in the presidency and to reverse the deterioration of executive power that had set in after <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Abraham_Lincoln" title="Assassination of Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln's death</a>. Although supporters have praised his commitment to civil service reform and defense of civil rights, Hayes is generally <a href="/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States" title="Historical rankings of Presidents of the United States">listed among the bottom half</a> in historians' rankings of U.S. presidents.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_and_early_life">Family and early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Family and early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Childhood_and_family_history">Childhood and family history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Childhood and family history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hayes_boyhood_home.PNG" class="image"><img alt="A two-story brick house" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Hayes_boyhood_home.PNG/220px-Hayes_boyhood_home.PNG" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Hayes_boyhood_home.PNG/330px-Hayes_boyhood_home.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Hayes_boyhood_home.PNG/440px-Hayes_boyhood_home.PNG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="393" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hayes_boyhood_home.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hayes's boyhood home in Delaware, Ohio</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rutherford Birchard Hayes was born in <a href="/wiki/Delaware,_Ohio" title="Delaware, Ohio">Delaware, Ohio</a>, on October 4, 1822, the son of Rutherford Hayes, Jr. and Sophia Birchard. Hayes's father, a <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a> storekeeper, took the family to Ohio in 1817. He died ten weeks before Rutherford's birth. Sophia took charge of the family, bringing up Hayes and his sister, Fanny, the only two of their four children to survive to adulthood.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom7.E2.80.938_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom7.E2.80.938-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> She never remarried;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom10Barnard76.E2.80.9377_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom10Barnard76.E2.80.9377-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Sophia's younger brother, Sardis Birchard, lived with the family for a time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse4_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse4-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> He was always close to Hayes and became a father figure to him, contributing to his early education.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom20.E2.80.9321Barnard27.E2.80.9331_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom20.E2.80.9321Barnard27.E2.80.9331-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Through both his father and mother, Hayes was of <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> colonial ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard41_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard41-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> His earliest American ancestor emigrated to <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a> from <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> in 1625.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse3_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse3-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes's great-grandfather, Ezekiel Hayes, was a militia captain in Connecticut in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, but Ezekiel's son (Hayes's grandfather, also named Rutherford) left his <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">New Haven</a> home during the war for the relative peace of Vermont.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard53_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard53-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> His mother's ancestors arrived in Vermont at a similar time, and most of his close relatives outside Ohio continued to live there. <a href="/wiki/John_Noyes" title="John Noyes">John Noyes</a>, an uncle by marriage, had been his father's business partner in Vermont and was later elected to Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom17.E2.80.9318_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom17.E2.80.9318-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> His first cousin, Mary Jane Noyes Mead, was the mother of sculptor <a href="/wiki/Larkin_Goldsmith_Mead" title="Larkin Goldsmith Mead">Larkin Goldsmith Mead</a> and architect <a href="/wiki/William_Rutherford_Mead" title="William Rutherford Mead">William Rutherford Mead</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom17.E2.80.9318_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom17.E2.80.9318-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Humphrey_Noyes" title="John Humphrey Noyes">John Humphrey Noyes</a>, the founder of the <a href="/wiki/Oneida_Community" title="Oneida Community">Oneida Community</a>, was also a first cousin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom62.E2.80.9363Barnard113_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom62.E2.80.9363Barnard113-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes' grandnephew was character actor <a href="/wiki/Grant_Mitchell_(actor)" title="Grant Mitchell (actor)">Grant Mitchell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> He became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Sons_of_the_American_Revolution" title="Sons of the American Revolution">Sons of the American Revolution</a> based on his descent from Daniel Austin and Elias Birchard.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_early_law_career">Education and early law career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Education and early law career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hayes attended the <a href="/wiki/Common_school" title="Common school">common schools</a> in Delaware, Ohio, and enrolled in 1836 at the <a href="/wiki/Methodist" title="Methodist" class="mw-redirect">Methodist</a> <a href="/wiki/Norwalk_Seminary" title="Norwalk Seminary">Norwalk Seminary</a> in <a href="/wiki/Norwalk,_Ohio" title="Norwalk, Ohio">Norwalk, Ohio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse4.E2.80.935_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse4.E2.80.935-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> He did well at Norwalk, and the following year transferred to a <a href="/wiki/University-preparatory_school" title="University-preparatory school">preparatory school</a> in <a href="/wiki/Middletown,_Connecticut" title="Middletown, Connecticut">Middletown</a>, Connecticut, where he studied <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom20.E2.80.9322Trefousse5_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom20.E2.80.9322Trefousse5-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Returning to Ohio, Hayes entered <a href="/wiki/Kenyon_College" title="Kenyon College">Kenyon College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gambier,_Ohio" title="Gambier, Ohio">Gambier</a> in 1838.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom25_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom25-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> He enjoyed his time at Kenyon, and was successful scholastically;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard107.E2.80.93113_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard107.E2.80.93113-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> while there, he joined several student societies and became interested in <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">Whig</a> politics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom33.E2.80.9343_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom33.E2.80.9343-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> He graduated with highest honors in 1842 and addressed the class as its <a href="/wiki/Valedictorian" title="Valedictorian">valedictorian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse6_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse6-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After briefly <a href="/wiki/Reading_law" title="Reading law">reading law</a> in <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus</a>, Ohio, Hayes moved east to attend <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Law_School" title="Harvard Law School">Harvard Law School</a> in 1843.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom43.E2.80.9351Barnard131.E2.80.93138_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom43.E2.80.9351Barnard131.E2.80.93138-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Graduating with an <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Laws" title="Bachelor of Laws">LL.B</a>, he was admitted to the Ohio <a href="/wiki/Bar_(law)" title="Bar (law)">bar</a> in 1845 and opened his own law office in Lower Sandusky (now <a href="/wiki/Fremont,_Ohio" title="Fremont, Ohio">Fremont</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom52.E2.80.9353_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom52.E2.80.9353-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Business was slow at first, but he gradually attracted a few clients and also represented his uncle Sardis in real estate litigation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom55.E2.80.9360_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom55.E2.80.9360-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1847, Hayes became ill with what his doctor thought to be <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>. Thinking a change in climate would help, he considered enlisting in the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a>, but on his doctor's advice he instead visited family in New England.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom62.E2.80.9366_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom62.E2.80.9366-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Returning from there, Hayes and his uncle Sardis made a long journey to <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, where Hayes visited with <a href="/wiki/Guy_M._Bryan" title="Guy M. Bryan">Guy M. Bryan</a>, a Kenyon classmate and distant relative.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom66.E2.80.9370Barnard114_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom66.E2.80.9370Barnard114-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Business remained meager on his return to Lower Sandusky, and Hayes decided to move to <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse8_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse8-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cincinnati_law_practice_and_marriage">Cincinnati law practice and marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Cincinnati law practice and marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rutherford_B._Hayes_and_his_wife.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Black-and-white picture of a man and a woman" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Rutherford_B._Hayes_and_his_wife.jpg/220px-Rutherford_B._Hayes_and_his_wife.jpg" width="220" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Rutherford_B._Hayes_and_his_wife.jpg/330px-Rutherford_B._Hayes_and_his_wife.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Rutherford_B._Hayes_and_his_wife.jpg/440px-Rutherford_B._Hayes_and_his_wife.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1172" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rutherford_B._Hayes_and_his_wife.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rutherford and Lucy Hayes on their wedding day</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hayes moved to Cincinnati in 1850, and opened a law office with John W. Herron, a lawyer from <a href="/wiki/Chillicothe,_Ohio" title="Chillicothe, Ohio">Chillicothe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom73_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom73-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>a<span>]</span></a></sup> Later, Herron joined a more established firm and Hayes formed a new partnership with William K. Rogers and Richard M. Corwine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard184.E2.80.93185_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard184.E2.80.93185-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> He found business better in Cincinnati, and enjoyed the social attractions of the larger city, joining the <a href="/wiki/Literary_Club_of_Cincinnati" title="Literary Club of Cincinnati">Cincinnati Literary Society</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Order_of_Odd_Fellows" title="Independent Order of Odd Fellows">Odd Fellows Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom74.E2.80.9375_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom74.E2.80.9375-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> He also attended the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">Episcopal Church</a> in Cincinnati but did not become a member.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom74.E2.80.9375_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom74.E2.80.9375-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Hayes courted his future wife, <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Webb_Hayes" title="Lucy Webb Hayes">Lucy Webb</a>, during his time there.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom78.E2.80.9386_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom78.E2.80.9386-28"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> His mother had encouraged him to get to know Lucy years earlier, but Hayes had believed she was too young and focused his attention on other women.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom61.E2.80.9362_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom61.E2.80.9362-29"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Four years later, Hayes began to spend more time with Lucy. They became engaged in 1851 and married on December 30, 1852, at the house of Lucy's mother.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom78.E2.80.9386_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom78.E2.80.9386-28"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Over the next five years, Lucy gave birth to three sons: Birchard Austin (1853), <a href="/wiki/Webb_Hayes" title="Webb Hayes">Webb Cook</a> (1856), and Rutherford Platt (1858).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard184.E2.80.93185_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard184.E2.80.93185-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Lucy, a <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodist</a>, was a <a href="/wiki/Teetotalism" title="Teetotalism">teetotaler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States" title="Abolitionism in the United States">abolitionist</a>. She influenced her husband's views on those issues, although he never formally joined her church.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard178.E2.80.93180.2C_187.E2.80.93188Hoogenboom93.E2.80.9395_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard178.E2.80.93180.2C_187.E2.80.93188Hoogenboom93.E2.80.9395-30"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Hayes had begun his law practice dealing primarily with commercial issues but won greater prominence in Cincinnati as a criminal defense attorney,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse9_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse9-31"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> defending several people accused of murder.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom87.E2.80.9393_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom87.E2.80.9393-32"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> In one case, he used a form of the <a href="/wiki/Insanity_defense" title="Insanity defense">insanity defense</a> that saved the accused from the <a href="/wiki/Gallows" title="Gallows">gallows</a>; the woman was instead confined to a mental institution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse10_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse10-33"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes also defended slaves who had escaped and were accused under the recently enacted <a href="/wiki/Fugitive_Slave_Act_of_1850" title="Fugitive Slave Act of 1850">Fugitive Slave Act of 1850</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom95.E2.80.9399Barnard189.E2.80.93191_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom95.E2.80.9399Barnard189.E2.80.93191-34"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> As Cincinnati was just across the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a> from <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, a slave state, it was a destination for escaping slaves and many such cases were tried in its courts. A staunch abolitionist, Hayes found his work on behalf of fugitive slaves personally gratifying as well as politically useful, as it raised his profile in the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarnard196.E2.80.93197Trefousse14.E2.80.9315_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarnard196.E2.80.93197Trefousse14.E2.80.9315-35"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>His political reputation rose with his professional plaudits. Hayes declined the Republican nomination for a judgeship in 1856.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom100_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom100-36"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Two years later, some Republicans proposed Hayes to fill a vacancy on the bench and he considered accepting the appointment until the office of <a href="/wiki/City_attorney" title="City attorney">city solicitor</a> also became vacant.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom104.E2.80.93105Barnard202.E2.80.93203_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom104.E2.80.93105Barnard202.E2.80.93203-37"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The city council elected Hayes as city solicitor to fill the vacancy, and he won a full two-year term from the voters in April 1859 with a larger majority than other Republicans on the <a href="/wiki/Ticket_(election)" title="Ticket (election)">ticket</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom107Barnard204_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom107Barnard204-38"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War">Civil War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Civil War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hayes_Civil_War.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A bearded man in a 19th-century army uniform" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Hayes_Civil_War.jpg/170px-Hayes_Civil_War.jpg" width="170" height="324" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Hayes_Civil_War.jpg/255px-Hayes_Civil_War.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Hayes_Civil_War.jpg/340px-Hayes_Civil_War.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="1333" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hayes_Civil_War.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hayes in Civil War uniform in 1861</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Virginia_and_South_Mountain">West Virginia and South Mountain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: West Virginia and South Mountain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As the Southern states started to secede after <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Lincoln</a>'s election to the Presidency in 1860, Hayes was lukewarm on the idea of a <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">civil war</a> to restore the Union. Considering that the two sides might be irreconcilable, he suggested that the Union "[l]et them go."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom113Barnard210_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom113Barnard210-39"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Although Ohio had voted for Lincoln in 1860, the Cincinnati voters turned against the Republican party after secession. Its residents included many from the South, and they voted for the Democrats and <a href="/wiki/Know-Nothing" title="Know-Nothing" class="mw-redirect">Know-Nothings</a>, who combined to sweep the city elections in April 1861, ejecting Hayes from the city solicitor's office.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom114Barnard210.E2.80.93212_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom114Barnard210.E2.80.93212-40"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Returning to private practice, Hayes formed a very brief law partnership with <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Markbreit" title="Leopold Markbreit">Leopold Markbreit</a>, lasting three days before the war began.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom114Barnard210.E2.80.93212_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom114Barnard210.E2.80.93212-40"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederates</a> had <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Sumter" title="Battle of Fort Sumter">fired on Fort Sumter</a>, Hayes resolved his doubts and joined a volunteer company composed of his Literary Society friends.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom115Barnard213.E2.80.93214_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom115Barnard213.E2.80.93214-41"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> That June, Governor <a href="/wiki/William_Dennison,_Jr." title="William Dennison, Jr." class="mw-redirect">William Dennison</a> appointed several of the officers of the volunteer company to positions in the <a href="/wiki/23rd_Ohio_Infantry" title="23rd Ohio Infantry">23rd Regiment of Ohio Volunteer Infantry</a>. Hayes was promoted to <a href="/wiki/Major_(United_States)" title="Major (United States)">major</a>, and his friend and college classmate <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Matthews_(lawyer)" title="Stanley Matthews (lawyer)">Stanley Matthews</a> was appointed <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_colonel_(United_States)" title="Lieutenant colonel (United States)">lieutenant colonel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom116.E2.80.93117_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom116.E2.80.93117-42"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Joining the regiment as a <a href="/wiki/Private_(rank)#United_States" title="Private (rank)">private</a> was <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">William McKinley</a>, another future president.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom116.E2.80.93117_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom116.E2.80.93117-42"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After a month of training, Hayes and the 23rd Ohio set out for western Virginia in July 1861 as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Kanawha_Division" title="Kanawha Division">Kanawha Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom120.E2.80.93121_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom120.E2.80.93121-43"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> They passed the next few months out of contact with the enemy until September, when the regiment encountered Confederates at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carnifex_Ferry" title="Battle of Carnifex Ferry">Carnifex Ferry</a> in present-day <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a> and drove them back.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom125.E2.80.93126Reid160_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom125.E2.80.93126Reid160-44"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> In November, Hayes was promoted to lieutenant colonel (Matthews having been promoted to colonel of another regiment) and led his troops deeper into western Virginia, where they entered winter quarters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom128.E2.80.93130_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom128.E2.80.93130-45"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The division resumed its advance the following spring, and Hayes led several raids against the rebel forces, on one of which he sustained a minor injury to his knee.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom136.E2.80.93141_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom136.E2.80.93141-46"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> That September, Hayes's regiment was called east to reinforce General <a href="/wiki/John_Pope_(military_officer)" title="John Pope (military officer)">John Pope</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Virginia" title="Army of Virginia">Army of Virginia</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Bull_Run" title="Second Battle of Bull Run">Second Battle of Bull Run</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom141.E2.80.93143_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom141.E2.80.93143-47"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Although Hayes and his troops did not arrive in time for the battle, they joined the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Potomac" title="Army of the Potomac">Army of the Potomac</a> as it hurried north to cut off <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">Robert E. Lee</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Northern_Virginia" title="Army of Northern Virginia">Army of Northern Virginia</a>, which was advancing into <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom141.E2.80.93143_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom141.E2.80.93143-47"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Marching north, the 23rd was the lead regiment encountering the Confederates at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_South_Mountain" title="Battle of South Mountain">Battle of South Mountain</a> on September 14.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom146.E2.80.93148_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom146.E2.80.93148-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes led a charge against an entrenched position and was shot through his left arm, fracturing the bone.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom146.E2.80.93147Reid161_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom146.E2.80.93147Reid161-49"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> He had one of his men tie a handkerchief above the wound in an effort to stop the bleeding, and continued to lead his men in the battle. While resting, he ordered his men to meet a flanking attack, but instead his entire command moved backward, leaving Hayes lying in between the lines.</p>
<p>Eventually, his men brought Hayes back behind their lines, and he was taken to hospital. The regiment continued on to <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Antietam" title="Battle of Antietam">Antietam</a>, but Hayes was out of action for the rest of the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom149.E2.80.93153_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom149.E2.80.93153-50"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> In October, he was promoted to <a href="/wiki/Colonel_(United_States)" title="Colonel (United States)">colonel</a> and assigned to command of the first brigade of the Kanawha Division as a <a href="/wiki/Brevet_(military)" title="Brevet (military)">brevet</a> <a href="/wiki/Brigadier_general_(United_States)" title="Brigadier general (United States)">brigadier general</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse30_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse30-51"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Army_of_the_Shenandoah">Army of the Shenandoah</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Army of the Shenandoah">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:George_Crook_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Black-and-white picture of a forked-bearded man in an army uniform" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/George_Crook_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/220px-George_Crook_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" width="220" height="289" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/George_Crook_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/330px-George_Crook_-_Brady-Handy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/George_Crook_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/440px-George_Crook_-_Brady-Handy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3024" data-file-height="3976" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:George_Crook_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/George_Crook" title="George Crook">George Crook</a> was Hayes's commander and the namesake of his fourth son</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The division spent the following winter and spring near <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_West_Virginia" title="Charleston, West Virginia">Charleston, Virginia</a> (present-day West Virginia), out of contact with the enemy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom154.E2.80.93156_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom154.E2.80.93156-52"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes saw little action until July 1863, when the division skirmished with <a href="/wiki/John_Hunt_Morgan" title="John Hunt Morgan">John Hunt Morgan</a>'s cavalry at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Buffington_Island" title="Battle of Buffington Island">Battle of Buffington Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom157.E2.80.93158_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom157.E2.80.93158-53"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Returning to Charleston for the rest of the summer, Hayes spent the fall encouraging the men of the 23rd Ohio to re-enlist, and many did so.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom159.E2.80.93161_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom159.E2.80.93161-54"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1864, the Army command structure in West Virginia was reorganized, and Hayes's division was assigned to <a href="/wiki/George_Crook" title="George Crook">George Crook</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Army_of_West_Virginia" title="Army of West Virginia">Army of West Virginia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom159.E2.80.93161_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom159.E2.80.93161-54"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Advancing into southwestern Virginia, they destroyed Confederate salt and lead mines there.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom162.E2.80.93164Trefousse32.E2.80.9333_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom162.E2.80.93164Trefousse32.E2.80.9333-55"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> On May 9, they engaged Confederate troops at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cloyd%27s_Mountain" title="Battle of Cloyd's Mountain">Cloyd's Mountain</a>, where Hayes and his men charged the enemy entrenchments and drove the rebels from the field.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom162.E2.80.93164Trefousse32.E2.80.9333_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom162.E2.80.93164Trefousse32.E2.80.9333-55"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the rout, the Union forces destroyed Confederate supplies and again successfully skirmished with the enemy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom162.E2.80.93164Trefousse32.E2.80.9333_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom162.E2.80.93164Trefousse32.E2.80.9333-55"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Hayes and his brigade moved to the <a href="/wiki/Shenandoah_Valley" title="Shenandoah Valley">Shenandoah Valley</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Valley_Campaigns_of_1864" title="Valley Campaigns of 1864">Valley Campaigns of 1864</a>. Crook's corps was attached to Major General <a href="/wiki/David_Hunter" title="David Hunter">David Hunter</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Union_Army_of_the_Shenandoah" title="Union Army of the Shenandoah">Army of the Shenandoah</a> and soon back in contact with Confederate forces, capturing <a href="/wiki/Lexington,_Virginia" title="Lexington, Virginia">Lexington, Virginia</a> on June 11.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom166.E2.80.93168_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom166.E2.80.93168-56"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> They continued south toward <a href="/wiki/Lynchburg,_Virginia" title="Lynchburg, Virginia">Lynchburg</a>, tearing up railroad track as they advanced.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom166.E2.80.93168_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom166.E2.80.93168-56"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> Hunter believed the troops at Lynchburg were too powerful, however, and Hayes and his brigade returned to West Virginia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom166.E2.80.93168_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom166.E2.80.93168-56"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes thought that Hunter lacked aggression, writing in a letter home that "General Crook would have taken Lynchburg."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom166.E2.80.93168_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom166.E2.80.93168-56"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> Before the army could make another attempt, Confederate General <a href="/wiki/Jubal_Early" title="Jubal Early">Jubal Early</a>'s raid into Maryland forced their recall to the north. Early's army surprised them at <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Kernstown" title="Second Battle of Kernstown">Kernstown</a> on July 24, where Hayes was slightly wounded by a bullet to the shoulder.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom168.E2.80.93169_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom168.E2.80.93169-57"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes also had a horse shot out from under him, and the army was defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom168.E2.80.93169_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom168.E2.80.93169-57"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Retreating into Maryland, the army was reorganized again, with Major General <a href="/wiki/Philip_Sheridan" title="Philip Sheridan">Philip Sheridan</a> replacing Hunter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom170.E2.80.93171_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom170.E2.80.93171-58"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> By August, Early was retreating up the valley, with Sheridan in pursuit. Hayes's troops fended off a Confederate assault at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berryville" title="Battle of Berryville">Berryville</a> and advanced to <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Opequon" title="Battle of Opequon" class="mw-redirect">Opequon Creek</a>, where they broke the enemy lines and pursued them farther south.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom172.E2.80.93173_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom172.E2.80.93173-59"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> They followed up the victory with another at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fisher%27s_Hill" title="Battle of Fisher's Hill">Fisher's Hill</a> on September 22, and one more at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cedar_Creek" title="Battle of Cedar Creek">Cedar Creek</a> on October 19.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom174.E2.80.93177_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom174.E2.80.93177-60"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> At Cedar Creek, Hayes sprained his ankle after being thrown from a horse and was struck in the head by a spent round, which did not cause serious damage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom174.E2.80.93177_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom174.E2.80.93177-60"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes's leadership and bravery drew the attention of his superiors, with <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Ulysses S. Grant</a> later writing of Hayes that "[h]is conduct on the field was marked by conspicuous gallantry as well as the display of qualities of a higher order than that of mere personal daring."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrant564_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrant564-61"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cedar Creek marked the end of the campaign. Hayes was promoted to <a href="/wiki/Brigadier_general_(United_States)" title="Brigadier general (United States)">brigadier general</a> in October 1864 and brevetted <a href="/wiki/Major_general_(United_States)" title="Major general (United States)">major general</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom178.E2.80.93181_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom178.E2.80.93181-62"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Around this time, Hayes learned of the birth of his son, George Crook Hayes. The army went into winter quarters once more, and in spring 1865 the war quickly came to a close with Lee's surrender to Grant at Appomattox. Hayes visited <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> that May and observed the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Review_of_the_Armies" title="Grand Review of the Armies">Grand Review of the Armies</a>, after which he and the 23rd Ohio returned to their home state to be mustered out of the service.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom186.E2.80.93188_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom186.E2.80.93188-63"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_politics">Post-war politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Post-war politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andrew_Johnson_photo_portrait_head_and_shoulders,_c1870-1880-Edit1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A photograph of a man in a black suit" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Andrew_Johnson_photo_portrait_head_and_shoulders%2C_c1870-1880-Edit1.jpg/180px-Andrew_Johnson_photo_portrait_head_and_shoulders%2C_c1870-1880-Edit1.jpg" width="180" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Andrew_Johnson_photo_portrait_head_and_shoulders%2C_c1870-1880-Edit1.jpg/270px-Andrew_Johnson_photo_portrait_head_and_shoulders%2C_c1870-1880-Edit1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Andrew_Johnson_photo_portrait_head_and_shoulders%2C_c1870-1880-Edit1.jpg/360px-Andrew_Johnson_photo_portrait_head_and_shoulders%2C_c1870-1880-Edit1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2050" data-file-height="2634" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andrew_Johnson_photo_portrait_head_and_shoulders,_c1870-1880-Edit1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pres. <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Johnson" title="Andrew Johnson">Andrew Johnson</a> and Republicans fought over Reconstruction</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Congressman">Congressman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Congressman">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While serving in the <a href="/wiki/Union_Army_of_the_Shenandoah" title="Union Army of the Shenandoah">Army of the Shenandoah</a> in 1864, Hayes was nominated by Republicans to run for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a> from <a href="/wiki/Ohio%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="Ohio's 2nd congressional district">Ohio's 2nd congressional district</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom171.E2.80.93176Barnard225.E2.80.93227_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom171.E2.80.93176Barnard225.E2.80.93227-64"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> Asked by friends in Cincinnati to leave the army to campaign, Hayes refused, saying that an "officer fit for duty who at this crisis would abandon his post to electioneer for a seat in Congress ought to be scalped."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom171.E2.80.93176Barnard225.E2.80.93227_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom171.E2.80.93176Barnard225.E2.80.93227-64"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> Instead, Hayes wrote several letters to the voters explaining his political positions and was elected by a 2,400-vote majority over the incumbent Democrat <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Long" title="Alexander Long">Alexander Long</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom171.E2.80.93176Barnard225.E2.80.93227_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom171.E2.80.93176Barnard225.E2.80.93227-64"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/39th_United_States_Congress" title="39th United States Congress">39th Congress</a> assembled in December 1865, Hayes was sworn in as a part of a large Republican majority. Hayes identified with the moderate wing of the party, but was willing to vote with the <a href="/wiki/Radical_Republicans" title="Radical Republicans" class="mw-redirect">radicals</a> for the sake of party unity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom200.E2.80.93201Conwell145.E2.80.93180_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom200.E2.80.93201Conwell145.E2.80.93180-65"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The major legislative effort of the Congress was the <a href="/wiki/Fourteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution</a>, for which Hayes voted and which passed both houses of Congress in June 1866.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom200.E2.80.93201Trefousse41.E2.80.9344Richardson17.E2.80.9318_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom200.E2.80.93201Trefousse41.E2.80.9344Richardson17.E2.80.9318-66"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes's beliefs were in line with his fellow Republicans on <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era_of_the_United_States" title="Reconstruction era of the United States" class="mw-redirect">Reconstruction</a> issues: that the South should be restored to the Union, but not without adequate protections for <a href="/wiki/Freedmen" title="Freedmen" class="mw-redirect">freedmen</a> and other black southerners.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom203Trefousse40.E2.80.9341_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom203Trefousse40.E2.80.9341-67"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Johnson" title="Andrew Johnson">Andrew Johnson</a>, who succeeded to office following Lincoln's assassination, to the contrary wanted to readmit the seceded states quickly without first ensuring that they adopted laws protecting the newly freed slaves' civil rights; he also granted pardons to many of the leading former Confederates.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom203Trefousse40.E2.80.9341_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom203Trefousse40.E2.80.9341-67"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes, along with congressional Republicans, disagreed. They worked to reject Johnson's vision of Reconstruction and to pass the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1866" title="Civil Rights Act of 1866">Civil Rights Act of 1866</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom197.E2.80.93199Trefousse42_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom197.E2.80.93199Trefousse42-68"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Re-elected in 1866, Hayes returned to the <a href="/wiki/Lame_duck_session_(United_States)" title="Lame duck session (United States)" class="mw-redirect">lame-duck session</a> to vote for the <a href="/wiki/Tenure_of_Office_Act_(1867)" title="Tenure of Office Act (1867)">Tenure of Office Act</a>, which ensured that Johnson could not remove administration officials without the Senate's consent.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom204.E2.80.93205_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom204.E2.80.93205-69"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> He also unsuccessfully pressed for a <a href="/wiki/United_States_civil_service" title="United States civil service" class="mw-redirect">civil service reform</a> bill that attracted the votes of many reform-minded Republicans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom204.E2.80.93205Foner493.E2.80.93494_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom204.E2.80.93205Foner493.E2.80.93494-70"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes continued to vote with the majority in the <a href="/wiki/40th_United_States_Congress" title="40th United States Congress">40th Congress</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Acts" title="Reconstruction Acts">Reconstruction Acts</a>, but resigned in July 1867 to campaign for governor of Ohio.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom208.E2.80.93210_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom208.E2.80.93210-71"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governor_of_Ohio">Governor of Ohio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Governor of Ohio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A popular Congressman and former Army officer, Hayes was considered by Ohio Republicans to be an excellent standard-bearer for the 1867 election campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom211.E2.80.93213Trefousse45.E2.80.9346_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom211.E2.80.93213Trefousse45.E2.80.9346-72"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes's political views were more moderate than the Republican party's platform, although he agreed with the proposed amendment to the Ohio state constitution that would guarantee <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">suffrage</a> to black Ohioans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom211.E2.80.93213Trefousse45.E2.80.9346_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom211.E2.80.93213Trefousse45.E2.80.9346-72"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes's opponent, <a href="/wiki/Allen_G._Thurman" title="Allen G. Thurman">Allen G. Thurman</a>, made the proposed amendment the centerpiece of the campaign, and both men campaigned vigorously, making speeches across the state, mostly focusing on the suffrage question.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom211.E2.80.93213Trefousse45.E2.80.9346_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom211.E2.80.93213Trefousse45.E2.80.9346-72"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The election was mostly a disappointment to Republicans, as the amendment failed to pass and Democrats gained a majority in the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_General_Assembly" title="Ohio General Assembly">state legislature</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom214Barnard238.E2.80.93239_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom214Barnard238.E2.80.93239-73"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes thought at first that he, too, had lost, but the final tally showed that he had won the election by 2,983 votes of 484,603 votes cast.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom214Barnard238.E2.80.93239_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom214Barnard238.E2.80.93239-73"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As a Republican governor with a Democratic legislature, Hayes had a limited role in governing, especially since <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Ohio" title="Governor of Ohio" class="mw-redirect">Ohio's governor</a> had no <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">veto</a> power. Despite these constraints, Hayes oversaw the establishment of a school for deaf-mutes and a reform school for girls.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse47.E2.80.9348_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse47.E2.80.9348-74"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> He endorsed the <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Andrew_Johnson" title="Impeachment of Andrew Johnson">impeachment of President Andrew Johnson</a> and urged his conviction, which failed by one vote in the United States Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom215.E2.80.93216_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom215.E2.80.93216-75"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Nominated for a second term in 1869, Hayes campaigned again for equal rights for black Ohioans and sought to associate his Democratic opponent, <a href="/wiki/George_H._Pendleton" title="George H. Pendleton">George H. Pendleton</a> with disunion and <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom218.E2.80.93220Barnard239.E2.80.93241_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom218.E2.80.93220Barnard239.E2.80.93241-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes was re-elected with an increased majority, and the Republicans took the legislature, ensuring Ohio's ratification of the <a href="/wiki/Fifteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fifteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Fifteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution</a>, which guaranteed black suffrage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom218.E2.80.93220Barnard239.E2.80.93241_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom218.E2.80.93220Barnard239.E2.80.93241-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> With a Republican legislature, Hayes's second term was more enjoyable. Suffrage was expanded and a state Agricultural and Mechanical College (later to become The <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_University" title="Ohio State University">Ohio State University</a>) established.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom225.E2.80.93228_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom225.E2.80.93228-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> He also proposed a reduction in state taxes and reform of the state prison system.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom231.E2.80.93232_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom231.E2.80.93232-78"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Choosing not to seek re-election, Hayes looked forward to retiring from politics in 1872.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom236.E2.80.93240_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom236.E2.80.93240-79"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Private_life_and_return_to_politics">Private life and return to politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Private life and return to politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spiegel_Grove_(Rutherford_B._Hayes_Summer_Home).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A large brick house surrounded by trees" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Spiegel_Grove_%28Rutherford_B._Hayes_Summer_Home%29.jpg/220px-Spiegel_Grove_%28Rutherford_B._Hayes_Summer_Home%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Spiegel_Grove_%28Rutherford_B._Hayes_Summer_Home%29.jpg/330px-Spiegel_Grove_%28Rutherford_B._Hayes_Summer_Home%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Spiegel_Grove_%28Rutherford_B._Hayes_Summer_Home%29.jpg/440px-Spiegel_Grove_%28Rutherford_B._Hayes_Summer_Home%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spiegel_Grove_(Rutherford_B._Hayes_Summer_Home).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hayes's home, <a href="/wiki/Spiegel_Grove" title="Spiegel Grove">Spiegel Grove</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Fremont,_Ohio" title="Fremont, Ohio">Fremont, Ohio</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As Hayes prepared to leave office, several delegations of reform-minded Republicans urged him to run against the incumbent Republican, <a href="/wiki/John_Sherman" title="John Sherman">John Sherman</a>, for <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom236.E2.80.93240_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom236.E2.80.93240-79"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes declined the offers, preferring to preserve party unity and retire to private life.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom236.E2.80.93240_79-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom236.E2.80.93240-79"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes especially looked forward to spending time with his children, two of whom (daughter Fanny and son Scott) had been born in the past five years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom241.E2.80.93242_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom241.E2.80.93242-80"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>b<span>]</span></a></sup> Initially, Hayes tried to promote railway extensions to his hometown, Fremont. He also managed some real estate he had acquired in <a href="/wiki/Duluth,_Minnesota" title="Duluth, Minnesota">Duluth, Minnesota</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom240.E2.80.93245Barnard250.E2.80.93252_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom240.E2.80.93245Barnard250.E2.80.93252-83"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Not entirely removed from politics, Hayes held out some hope of a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Cabinet" title="United States Cabinet" class="mw-redirect">cabinet</a> appointment, but was disappointed to receive only an appointment as assistant U.S. treasurer at Cincinnati, which he turned down.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom246.E2.80.93248_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom246.E2.80.93248-84"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> He agreed to be nominated for his old House seat in 1872 but was not disappointed when he lost the election to <a href="/wiki/Henry_B._Banning" title="Henry B. Banning">Henry B. Banning</a>, a fellow <a href="/wiki/Kenyon_College" title="Kenyon College">Kenyon College</a> alumnus.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom243.E2.80.93244Barnard250.E2.80.93252_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom243.E2.80.93244Barnard250.E2.80.93252-85"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1873, Lucy gave birth to another son, Manning Force Hayes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom249.E2.80.93250_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom249.E2.80.93250-86"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>c<span>]</span></a></sup> That same year, the <a href="/wiki/Panic_of_1873" title="Panic of 1873">Panic of 1873</a> hurt business prospects across the nation, including Hayes's. Sardis Birchard died that year and the Hayes family moved into <a href="/wiki/Spiegel_Grove" title="Spiegel Grove">Spiegel Grove</a>, the grand house Birchard had built with them in mind.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom249.E2.80.93251_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom249.E2.80.93251-89"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Hayes hoped to remain out of politics in order to pay off the debts he had incurred during the Panic, but when the Republican state convention nominated him for governor in 1875, he accepted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom256.E2.80.93257Barnard270.E2.80.93271_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom256.E2.80.93257Barnard270.E2.80.93271-90"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> The campaign against Democratic nominee <a href="/wiki/William_Allen_(governor)" title="William Allen (governor)">William Allen</a> focused primarily on Protestant fears of the possibility of <a href="/wiki/Blaine_Amendment" title="Blaine Amendment">state aid to Catholic schools</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom257.E2.80.93260Barnard271.E2.80.93275Foner557_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom257.E2.80.93260Barnard271.E2.80.93275Foner557-91"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes was against such funding and, while he was not known to be personally <a href="/wiki/Anti-Catholic" title="Anti-Catholic" class="mw-redirect">anti-Catholic</a>, he allowed anti-Catholic fervor to contribute to the enthusiasm for his candidacy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom257.E2.80.93260Barnard271.E2.80.93275Foner557_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom257.E2.80.93260Barnard271.E2.80.93275Foner557-91"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> The campaign was a success, and Hayes was returned to the governorship by a 5,544-vote majority.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom257.E2.80.93260Barnard271.E2.80.93275Foner557_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom257.E2.80.93260Barnard271.E2.80.93275Foner557-91"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_of_1876">Election of 1876</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Election of 1876">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1876" title="United States presidential election, 1876">United States presidential election, 1876</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republican_nomination_and_campaign_against_Tilden">Republican nomination and campaign against Tilden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Republican nomination and campaign against Tilden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hayes-Wheeler.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Sepia-toned picture of two men; one bearded, one clean-shaven" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Hayes-Wheeler.jpg/220px-Hayes-Wheeler.jpg" width="220" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Hayes-Wheeler.jpg/330px-Hayes-Wheeler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Hayes-Wheeler.jpg/440px-Hayes-Wheeler.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3011" data-file-height="4147" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hayes-Wheeler.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hayes-Wheeler campaign poster</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hayes's success in Ohio immediately elevated him to the top ranks of Republican politicians under consideration for the presidency in 1876.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse62_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse62-92"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> The Ohio delegation to the <a href="/wiki/1876_Republican_National_Convention" title="1876 Republican National Convention">1876 Republican National Convention</a> was united behind him, and Senator <a href="/wiki/John_Sherman" title="John Sherman">John Sherman</a> did all in his power to bring Hayes the nomination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom260.E2.80.93261Robinson57_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom260.E2.80.93261Robinson57-93"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 1876, the convention assembled with <a href="/wiki/James_G._Blaine" title="James G. Blaine">James G. Blaine</a> of <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> as the favorite.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom262.E2.80.93263Robinson53.E2.80.9355_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom262.E2.80.93263Robinson53.E2.80.9355-94"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Blaine started with a significant lead in the delegate count but could not muster a majority. As he failed to gain votes, the delegates looked elsewhere for a nominee and settled on Hayes on the seventh ballot.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom263.E2.80.93264Robinson61.E2.80.9363_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom263.E2.80.93264Robinson61.E2.80.9363-95"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The convention then selected Representative <a href="/wiki/William_A._Wheeler" title="William A. Wheeler">William A. Wheeler</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a> for Vice President, a man about whom Hayes had recently asked, "I am ashamed to say: who is Wheeler?"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom260Robinson63_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom260Robinson63-96"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Democratic nominee was <a href="/wiki/Samuel_J._Tilden" title="Samuel J. Tilden">Samuel J. Tilden</a>, the Governor of New York. Tilden was considered a formidable adversary who, like Hayes, had a reputation for honesty.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson64.E2.80.9368.2C_90.E2.80.9395_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson64.E2.80.9368.2C_90.E2.80.9395-97"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Also like Hayes, Tilden was a <a href="/wiki/Gold_standard" title="Gold standard">hard-money</a> man and supported civil service reform.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson64.E2.80.9368.2C_90.E2.80.9395_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson64.E2.80.9368.2C_90.E2.80.9395-97"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> In accordance with the custom of the time, the campaign was conducted by surrogates, with Hayes and Tilden remaining in their respective home towns.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson97.E2.80.9398_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson97.E2.80.9398-98"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> The poor economic conditions made the party in power unpopular and made Hayes suspect that he might lose the election.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse71_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse71-99"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Both candidates focused their attention on the swing states of <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>, as well as the three southern states—<a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>—where <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era_of_the_United_States" title="Reconstruction era of the United States" class="mw-redirect">Reconstruction</a> governments still barely ruled, amid recurring political violence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse72.E2.80.9373Robinson113.E2.80.93114_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse72.E2.80.9373Robinson113.E2.80.93114-100"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> The Republicans emphasized the danger of letting Democrats run the nation so soon after southern Democrats provoked the Civil War and, to a lesser extent, the danger a Democratic administration would pose to the recently won civil rights of southern blacks.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom269.E2.80.93271_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom269.E2.80.93271-101"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> Democrats, for their part, trumpeted Tilden's record of reform and contrasted it with the <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant_presidential_administration_scandals" title="Ulysses S. Grant presidential administration scandals">corruption of the incumbent Grant administration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson99.E2.80.93102_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson99.E2.80.93102-102"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As the returns were tallied on election day, it was clear that the race was close: Democrats had carried most of the South, as well as New York, Indiana, <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse74_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse74-103"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> In the Northeast, an increasing number of immigrants and their descendants voted Democratic. The popular vote also favored Tilden, but Republicans realized that if they held the three <a href="/wiki/Redeemers" title="Redeemers">unredeemed</a> southern states together with some of the western states, they would emerge with an <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">electoral college</a> majority.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse75Robinson119.E2.80.93123_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse75Robinson119.E2.80.93123-104"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disputed_electoral_votes">Disputed electoral votes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Disputed electoral votes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Compromise_of_1877" title="Compromise of 1877">Compromise of 1877</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_States)" title="Electoral Commission (United States)">Electoral Commission (United States)</a></div>
<p>On November 11, three days after election day, Tilden appeared to have won 184 electoral votes: one short of a majority.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson126.E2.80.93127_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson126.E2.80.93127-105"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Hayes appeared to have 166 votes, with the 19 votes of Florida, Louisiana, and South Carolina still in doubt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson126.E2.80.93127_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson126.E2.80.93127-105"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Republicans and Democrats each claimed victory in the three latter states, but the results in those states were rendered uncertain because of fraud by both parties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson131.E2.80.93142Hoogenboom277.E2.80.93279_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson131.E2.80.93142Hoogenboom277.E2.80.93279-106"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> To further complicate matters, one of the three electors from <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a> (a state Hayes had won) was disqualified, reducing Hayes's total to 165, and raising the disputed votes to 20. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson127.E2.80.93128_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson127.E2.80.93128-107"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>d<span>]</span></a></sup> If either candidate could be awarded the 20 disputed votes, he would be elected president.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ElectoralCollege1876.svg" class="image"><img alt="A map of the United States showing electoral results in 1876" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/ElectoralCollege1876.svg/300px-ElectoralCollege1876.svg.png" width="300" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/ElectoralCollege1876.svg/450px-ElectoralCollege1876.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/ElectoralCollege1876.svg/600px-ElectoralCollege1876.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1020" data-file-height="593" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ElectoralCollege1876.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Results of the 1876 election, with states won by Hayes in <span style="color:red">red</span>, and those won by Tilden in <span style="color:blue">blue</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There was considerable debate about which person or house of Congress was authorized to decide between the competing slates of electors, with the Republican Senate and the Democratic House each claiming priority.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson145.E2.80.93154Hoogenboom281.E2.80.93286_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson145.E2.80.93154Hoogenboom281.E2.80.93286-110"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> By January 1877, with the question still unresolved, Congress and President <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Grant</a> agreed to submit the matter to a bipartisan <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_States)" title="Electoral Commission (United States)">Electoral Commission</a>, which would be authorized to determine the fate of the disputed electoral votes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson157_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson157-111"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> The Commission was to be made up of five <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">representatives</a>, five <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">senators</a>, and five <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court justices</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson158_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson158-112"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> To ensure partisan balance, there would be seven Democrats and seven Republicans, with Justice <a href="/wiki/David_Davis_(Supreme_Court_justice)" title="David Davis (Supreme Court justice)">David Davis</a>, an independent respected by both parties, as the fifteenth member.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson158_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson158-112"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The balance was upset when Democrats in the <a href="/wiki/Illinois_State_Legislature" title="Illinois State Legislature" class="mw-redirect">Illinois legislature</a> elected Davis to the Senate, hoping to sway his vote.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom286_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom286-113"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Davis disappointed Democrats by refusing to serve on the Commission because of his election to the Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom286_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom286-113"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> As all of the remaining Justices were Republicans, Justice <a href="/wiki/Joseph_P._Bradley" title="Joseph P. Bradley">Joseph P. Bradley</a>, believed to be the most independent-minded of them, was selected to take Davis's place on the Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson159.E2.80.93161_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson159.E2.80.93161-114"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> The Commission met in February and the eight Republicans voted to award all 20 electoral votes to Hayes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson166.E2.80.93171_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson166.E2.80.93171-115"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> Democrats were outraged by the result and attempted a <a href="/wiki/Filibuster" title="Filibuster">filibuster</a> to prevent Congress from accepting the Commission's findings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson171.E2.80.93183_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson171.E2.80.93183-116"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As the March 4 inauguration day neared, Republican and Democratic Congressional leaders met at <a href="/wiki/Wormley%27s_Hotel" title="Wormley's Hotel">Wormley's Hotel</a> in Washington to negotiate a <a href="/wiki/Compromise_of_1877" title="Compromise of 1877">compromise</a>. Republicans promised concessions in exchange for Democratic acquiescence in the Committee's decision. The primary concession Hayes promised would be the withdrawal of federal troops from the South and an acceptance of the election of Democratic governments in the remaining "unredeemed" states of the South.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson182.E2.80.93184Foner580.E2.80.93581_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson182.E2.80.93184Foner580.E2.80.93581-117"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The Democrats agreed, and on March 2, the filibuster was ended. Hayes was elected, but Reconstruction was finished.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson185.E2.80.93189Foner581.E2.80.93587_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson185.E2.80.93189Foner581.E2.80.93587-118"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidency_1877.E2.80.931881">Presidency 1877–1881</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Presidency 1877–1881">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inauguration">Inauguration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rutherford_B._Hayes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Inauguration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
